  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4e92597b-99d4-4248-b2a8-3932918727de'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10646354322092328706">In the realm of Faerie, the time has come for Roiben's coronation. Uneasy in the midst of the malevolent Unseelie Court, pixie Kaye is sure of only one thing -- her love for Roiben.   <span id="freeText10646354322092328706" style="display:none">In the realm of Faerie, the time has come for Roiben's coronation. Uneasy in the midst of the malevolent Unseelie Court, pixie Kaye is sure of only one thing -- her love for Roiben. But when Kaye, drunk on faerie wine, declares herself to Roiben, he sends her on a seemingly impossible quest. Now Kaye can't see or speak to Roiben unless she can find the one thing she knows doesn't exist: a faerie who can tell a lie. <br /><br /> Miserable and convinced she belongs nowhere, Kaye decides to tell her mother the truth -- that she is a changeling left in place of the human daughter stolen long ago. Her mother's shock and horror sends Kaye back to the world of Faerie to find her human counterpart and return her to Ironside. But once back in the faerie courts, Kaye finds herself a pawn in the games of Silarial, queen of the Seelie Court. Silarial wants Roiben's throne, and she will use Kaye, and any means necessary, to get it. In this game of wits and weapons, can a pixie outplay a queen? <br /><br /> Holly Black spins a seductive tale at once achingly real and chillingly enchanted, set in a dangerous world where pleasure mingles with pain and nothing is exactly as it appears.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10646354322092328706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

It's the weakest of the three and nothing relevant happens in it. You'll read the third book and wonder who these characters are who are mentioned in passing, but you don't need to know and the answers aren't very interesting anyway.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1409574040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409574040" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409574040?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781847380630" href="/book/show/3942410-ironside">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409574040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15297005729220929242">It only took to the last book of the trilogy buuuuuut....<b>I LOVED THIS ONE SO MUCH!</b> It's like <i>the</i> Holly Black style that I adore and it's everything that I wanted and it's immensely faerieish and creepy and cruel and dark and WELL I AM A PLEASED SPRITE.<br/><br/>...although I have to admit, book 2, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales___2_' title='Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales, #2) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Valiant</a> still makes exactly zero sense. It was about Luis, who has a part in this book, but it was narrated by Val, who has NO PART IN THIS BOOK WHATSOEVER. Random and odd? I thinkee yes.<br/><br/>ANYWAY.<br/><br/><b>I loved how creep</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15297005729220929242" style="display:none">It only took to the last book of the trilogy buuuuuut....<b>I LOVED THIS ONE SO MUCH!</b> It's like <i>the</i> Holly Black style that I adore and it's everything that I wanted and it's immensely faerieish and creepy and cruel and dark and WELL I AM A PLEASED SPRITE.<br /><br />...although I have to admit, book 2, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales___2_" title="Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a> still makes exactly zero sense. It was about Luis, who has a part in this book, but it was narrated by Val, who has NO PART IN THIS BOOK WHATSOEVER. Random and odd? I thinkee yes.<br /><br />ANYWAY.<br /><br /><b>I loved how creepily dark this was.</b> It's set more in the faerie worlds. And, yeeeah, the plot was a bit painful, aka, it consisted of Roiban saying "DON'T DO THE THING" and Kaye going "BUT I WANNA DO THE THING" and blood everywhere and regret and bad faerie food. BUT! It was still interesting and never slow and I loved how delicious the writing was. I felt really sucked into the story.<br /><br />Oh and the characters? <b>I've been a bit BLEH and MEH with the characters....up until this book. Now I love them.</b> Weeell...I LOVE CORNY. Omg, Corny is one of the most perfect characters of <i>ever</i>. He's funny and sarcastic and he also has a dark side. Like <i>really</i> dark. I really loved this about him because he was so complex and interesting. Whereas Kaye was all <i>love! and freedom! and truth! and belonging!</i> and blah blah, Kaye we get it, you're having a crisis. And while Kaye and Roiban's relationship was built on "protecting" each other by shunning each other...we have Corny's crush on Luis which. was. adorable. OMG I SHIP IT SO HARD.<br /><br /><b>There is plenty of death and torture and destruction too.</b> I'm not a sadist but YAY!! The book promises darkness and <i>comes through with it</i>. SO BE PREPARED FOR SOME SMUSHED FEELS. Bad stuff goes down and people get hurt and blood everywhere. And swords!<br /><br />AND IT'S FUNNY. YAY AND THANK YOU.<br /><br />I binge read this trilogy in like, um, 3 days, so I can safely say <b>I did enjoy it, although the start was rocky.</b> I'm totally sad it's over too. I think I've read all the Holly Black books now?!? Um, WHAT DO I DO WITH MY LIFE, HUH!??!? I WANT MORE CREEPY FAERIE BOOKS...</span>
  <a data-text-id="15297005729220929242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2731392127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2731392127" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2731392127?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=2020faves">2020faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-pn-urban-fantasy">sff-pn-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=2020reads">2020reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2731392127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10386084567639693214">It’s not often that a series conclusion elevates a series to another level. This does. <br/><br/>In <i>Ironside</i>, the conclusion to the Modern Faerie Tales series, Roiben sends Kaye on an impossible quest, and Kaye must come to terms with her identity between faerie and human worlds. <br/><br/><i>Ironside</i>’s biggest success is in its newfound development of characters who didn’t feel as if they had internal lives earlier. Specifically, Corny, who came off like a gay best friend trope in the first book, has a far more inter</span>
  <span id="freeText10386084567639693214" style="display:none">It’s not often that a series conclusion elevates a series to another level. This does. <br /><br />In <i>Ironside</i>, the conclusion to the Modern Faerie Tales series, Roiben sends Kaye on an impossible quest, and Kaye must come to terms with her identity between faerie and human worlds. <br /><br /><i>Ironside</i>’s biggest success is in its newfound development of characters who didn’t feel as if they had internal lives earlier. Specifically, Corny, who came off like a gay best friend trope in the first book, has a far more interesting arc here. In the first book, he’s used as a prop until the ending, and feels lacking in internal life. Here, he’s dynamic, with an arc around trauma and revenge that is genuinely resonant. He and Liam from book two also start a romantic relationship that feels… surprisingly well-built? There’s this one scene between the two—<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[running water, salt <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>—that I genuinely can’t stop thinking about. <br /><br />The development of Ellen, Kaye’s mother, was likewise really interesting. Kaye’s first book characterization could have done with better focus on this relationship, which was flawed from the beginning. Here, the relationship between the two is put towards Kaye’s growth, her acceptance of herself as both faerie and somehow human. <br /><br />The plot here feels simultaneously just as brutal and more <b>twisty</b> than previous books, which I enjoyed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And the solution to the plot of this is a PUN, which… excellent. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Holly Black has definitely improved a lot as an author since writing this series in general, but this series conclusion was good. I don’t know if I’d tell <i>everyone</i> to take their time and read this series, but if you’re a fan of Holly Black’s other work, I’d encourage you to go for it. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://thebookishactress.carrd.co/" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a> | </span>
  <a data-text-id="10386084567639693214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1896910130289941667"><b>Loved this book!</b><br/><br/><i>Ironside</i> is the third installment of the <i>Modern Faerie Tales</i> series. I just love this dark and creepy series. Learning about the faerie world just keeps getting interesting and interesting. However, I'm still just wondering why the food is never good? Or is that just me...<br/><br/>Now in this book, you will meet and fall in love with Corny. He was definitely amazing and perfect in my eyes. Any character that speaks sarcasm will always connect with me. ALWAYS. Yeah, that's pretty much it. </span>
  <span id="freeText1896910130289941667" style="display:none"><b>Loved this book!</b><br /><br /><i>Ironside</i> is the third installment of the <i>Modern Faerie Tales</i> series. I just love this dark and creepy series. Learning about the faerie world just keeps getting interesting and interesting. However, I'm still just wondering why the food is never good? Or is that just me...<br /><br />Now in this book, you will meet and fall in love with Corny. He was definitely amazing and perfect in my eyes. Any character that speaks sarcasm will always connect with me. ALWAYS. Yeah, that's pretty much it. Kaye and Roiban were just meh to me. I hate their constant push and pull kind of relationship. Kaye just seems to always be in a crisis or something. I was just so done with their meh relationship. <br /><br />Besides all of that, there's a crap ton of death, torture, and destruction in this book. Again, I love the darkness in these books. Maybe it brings out the darker side of me but yeah, it was funny and a really enjoyable read. I'm happy that I finally got a chance to dive into this book and I can't wait to dive into another book by Holly.</span>

  <span id="freeText11086752077930849654" style="display:none">I loved this one just as much as Tithe! I like how we get a sort of collision with Luis from book two and get to learn more about him. Also, loved him and Corny!<br /><br />Kaye has really grown as a character. She is strong and brave and fierce, and I love her, too! I wish there would have been more of Roiben, but the scenes that he was in were awesome!<br /><br />Again, Holly Black has created such a magnificent world where character's feel real because they may not be a hundred percent likeable yet are! Highly recommend this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11086752077930849654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9170445941734411362">2.75 stars<br/><br/>I suppose this is a solid end to this trilogy, but it was my least favorite book of the three and this series in general is one of my least favorites by Holly Black. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629010335' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thoughts on Book #1, Tithe.</a> <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3509015341' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thoughts on Book #2, Valiant.</a><br/><br/>This is another reaction review, folks, so please check the book description if you want more detailed info! <br/><br/>Okay, so Ironside wasn't exactly what I expected—or, to be brutal, even wanted—for the end of this trilogy. That sounds dramatic. It was fine. But I wanted mo</span>
  <span id="freeText9170445941734411362" style="display:none">2.75 stars<br /><br />I suppose this is a solid end to this trilogy, but it was my least favorite book of the three and this series in general is one of my least favorites by Holly Black. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629010335" rel="nofollow noopener">Thoughts on Book #1, Tithe.</a> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3509015341" rel="nofollow noopener">Thoughts on Book #2, Valiant.</a><br /><br />This is another reaction review, folks, so please check the book description if you want more detailed info! <br /><br />Okay, so Ironside wasn't exactly what I expected—or, to be brutal, even wanted—for the end of this trilogy. That sounds dramatic. It was fine. But I wanted more, and what I got I wanted less of. <br /><br />First off, I think it's hard to have a series where the first book follows one set of characters, the second book follows another set of characters, and then the third book cherry-picks which of those two sets of characters to include—instead of wrapping up the plot lines of ALL the characters. It leaves me, the reader, with confused vibe. I thought we'd get an almost 50/50 split of the main characters of Tithe and the main characters of Valiant, but this really wasn't the case. That bothered me. <br /><br />I was also irked by the choices made in terms of how the final endgame went down. In a typical move for this series, lots of time and descriptions were spent on the random fillers of the series—the gritty realities of urban city life, the mundane day-to-day, the weird teenager dialogue. When you have a "final showdown" between two faerie courts, I was expecting us to cover that portion with more detail and pages....not spend 75% of the book on the same stuff that the first two books covered. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_21683340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21683340" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21683340?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-gold-star-award-winner">trt-gold-star-award-winner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21683340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13764365381483706547">Reviewed by Andie Z. for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>I have been looking forward to this book ever since I finished TITHE, and Holly Black most definitely does not disappoint. IRONSIDE picks up soon after the events in TITHE and VALIANT, and takes the reader on another breathless journey into the amazing and deadly world of Faerie. <br/><br/>Things have been uneasy ever since Roiben assumed the throne of the Unseelie Court, and with the threat of war in the air and Roiben's coronation drawing near, everyone is on edg</span>
  <span id="freeText13764365381483706547" style="display:none">Reviewed by Andie Z. for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />I have been looking forward to this book ever since I finished TITHE, and Holly Black most definitely does not disappoint. IRONSIDE picks up soon after the events in TITHE and VALIANT, and takes the reader on another breathless journey into the amazing and deadly world of Faerie. <br /><br />Things have been uneasy ever since Roiben assumed the throne of the Unseelie Court, and with the threat of war in the air and Roiben's coronation drawing near, everyone is on edge. Changeling Kaye Fierch knows that she loves Roiben, but she feels increasingly unwelcome and out of place in the Unseelie Court. So the night of the coronation, determined to prove herself to Roiben and the rest of the court, she makes a formal declaration and pledges herself to him as his consort. However, faerie custom demands that a quest be undertaken before anyone can sit as the Lord's consort, and Roiben grants Kaye an impossible task: to find a fairy who can tell an untruth. Now she is forbidden from seeing or speaking to him until she completes something she knows cannot be done. <br /><br />Kaye doesn't know where to go, because she has been feeling uncomfortable at home as well, knowing that she stole a human child's life. In a moment of desperation, she tells her mother the truth: that she is a changeling that was switched with Ellen's real daughter, the real Kaye, and she vows to retrieve her from the Seelie Court and return her to Ellen. She feels that this, at least, is something she can do, even if there's no way she can complete Roiben's quest. <br /><br />But with all the tension between the courts there is nowhere safe, and in venturing into the Seelie Court to find her human counterpart, Kaye puts herself within reach of Lady Silarial. Silarial wants Roiben's throne, and she's willing to do anything, including using Kaye, to get it. Once again Kaye finds herself in the middle of Faerie politics, but this time Roiben's not there to save her, and she may not have a way out. <br /><br />In my personal experience it is rare that a sequel ever lives up to the first book, but IRONSIDE does just that. Full of court rivalry, deception and betrayal, sword fights and murder, faerie curses, new romances, and even characters from VALIANT, IRONSIDE is another wonderful foray into the dark, gritty world of Faerie and will not leave readers disappointed. It will make you laugh, it will make you cry, it will make you pound your pillow in frustration and clap your hands in delight. My one and only complaint is that this is the last book set in this amazing world. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13764365381483706547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_225303111" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225303111" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225303111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16405878100814968844">This was nearly as good as the first book, which is my favourite in this series. It had an actual quest and adventure, like the first. But it focused mostly on Kaye, Corny, and Luis (a returning character from book 2), and not enough Roiben. And there was very little romance. The most sexually charged scene was actually between two supporting characters. It was brief but you could tell it was heated. I wouldn't have been disappointed if we had seen more of them. This book remains primarily a fae</span>
  <span id="freeText16405878100814968844" style="display:none">This was nearly as good as the first book, which is my favourite in this series. It had an actual quest and adventure, like the first. But it focused mostly on Kaye, Corny, and Luis (a returning character from book 2), and not enough Roiben. And there was very little romance. The most sexually charged scene was actually between two supporting characters. It was brief but you could tell it was heated. I wouldn't have been disappointed if we had seen more of them. This book remains primarily a faerie adventure. In that sense it was very good. Lots of action and suspense and faerie politics. <br /><br />Although Luis was in this one, and a glimpse of Val and Ravus at the end, the story of the second book was not relevant to this one, and anything you would have to know about Luis was explained in this one. So you could read just #1 and 3, or just #2 alone, if you wanted to. But just read them all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16405878100814968844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1107791579040308708">I'm very fresh out of all the Modern Faerie Tales by Holly Black, and I have to say that this garnered the most bland reaction from me, even though I think it stands on par with the others rating-wise.<br/><br/>It has no major flaws that I can really highlight, it just wasn't endowed with the most engaging plot, in my opinion. I wasn't very invested in Kaye's quest for Roiben <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ or her "sister" <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I could predict from early on Silarial's plot.   <span id="freeText1107791579040308708" style="display:none">I'm very fresh out of all the Modern Faerie Tales by Holly Black, and I have to say that this garnered the most bland reaction from me, even though I think it stands on par with the others rating-wise.<br /><br />It has no major flaws that I can really highlight, it just wasn't endowed with the most engaging plot, in my opinion. I wasn't very invested in Kaye's quest for Roiben <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ or her "sister" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I could predict from early on Silarial's plot. While I loved to spend time again with the characters from both Tithe and Valiant (though I would've liked more Ravus and Val), I think that was really the highlight of this book. I didn't find Kaye's POV interesting for this story, and as she even pointed out in the middle of the book, she didn't feel like the main character in this either.<br /><br />I'm being perhaps picky here, but all of this to say that this book just didn't engage me as much as the others and wasn't very interesting plot-wise.<br /><br />What was interesting, again, were the characters and the interactions between those from "different books"! There were some moments of expanded world-building as well (namely with the declarations of love and the quest), but these were sparse nonetheless.</span>

<div id="review_2425104086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425104086" />
    <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos"><img alt="Julie Zantopoulos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503178209p2/51094260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2425104086?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Zantopoulos" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos">Julie Zantopoulos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425104086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6499564056033869515">Just like Tithe, this story is an OG Fae story so I love it for that alone and have to say that this one held up a lot better than Tithe did. Of course, Holly's writing had only improved over the years but for being twelve years old, this story was super enjoyable, diverse, and just the right amount of dark. <br/><br/>I read this as a direct sequel to Tithe (skipping Valient) and didn't find that I was confused or missing information. This story was richly woven in terms of Fae court intrigue, romance, an</span>
  <span id="freeText6499564056033869515" style="display:none">Just like Tithe, this story is an OG Fae story so I love it for that alone and have to say that this one held up a lot better than Tithe did. Of course, Holly's writing had only improved over the years but for being twelve years old, this story was super enjoyable, diverse, and just the right amount of dark. <br /><br />I read this as a direct sequel to Tithe (skipping Valient) and didn't find that I was confused or missing information. This story was richly woven in terms of Fae court intrigue, romance, and even addiction and the desire to be different than you were born to be. We have Corny wishing he was Fae, Kaye wishing that she could be a true daughter to Ellen, and Rioben trying to find a way to avoid war between the Bright and Dark courts. There's a lot going on, a bunch of storylines to juggle, and Black does it really well. <br /><br />I loved the introduction of a few new characters and oh man...even those "bright" fae are just a**holes sometimes. Of course, Rioben steals the show for me as does Corny and his desire to be Fae like Kaye. Another great Holly Black Fae story to add to my shelves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6499564056033869515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10192613412099452753">Honestly, I don't know why I keep reading Holly Black, because even while I enjoyed this -- and it was enjoyable; if you liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_' title='Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales___2_' title='Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales, #2) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Valiant</a>, you'll enjoy this one -- I always find myself ending up <i>annoyed</i> by her books, which overrides any enjoyment I get out of them. I don't know, I just feel like her books are too <i>coy</i>, like they're full of inside jokes that I don't get, and okay, you know what, that's fine, she can put all the inside jokes she wants in her books, but when her readers feel a</span>
  <span id="freeText10192613412099452753" style="display:none">Honestly, I don't know why I keep reading Holly Black, because even while I enjoyed this -- and it was enjoyable; if you liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_" title="Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales___2_" title="Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a>, you'll enjoy this one -- I always find myself ending up <i>annoyed</i> by her books, which overrides any enjoyment I get out of them. I don't know, I just feel like her books are too <i>coy</i>, like they're full of inside jokes that I don't get, and okay, you know what, that's fine, she can put all the inside jokes she wants in her books, but when her readers feel alienated because of them, when they actively read her books and feel like they're left out of the cool kids club, that's a bad thing. And that's always how I end up feeling when I read a Holly Black novel, and, yes, I feel guilty and mean for feeling that, but it doesn't change the fact that I <i>feel</i> it in the first place.<br /><br /><b>Edit:</b> Holy cow, people, this review is FIVE YEARS OLD - I have no idea what I meant, I gave up reading Holly Black shortly after this book because I just personally didn't enjoy her books, I seriously can't answer any questions about this.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16002139171109517118">Holly Black is an amazing writer, no matter which series you’re reading. Her writing is sooooo atmospheric, immersive and dark you can almost feel the chill in the air and smell crispy leaves 🍁 Nor does she shy away from portraying the dark side of humanity.<br/><br/>This was by far my <i>favorite</i> book of the series and I enjoyed every bit of it! <br/><br/>I loved the close friendship between Kaye and Corny, and their shared grief of Janet.   <span id="freeText16002139171109517118" style="display:none">Holly Black is an amazing writer, no matter which series you’re reading. Her writing is sooooo atmospheric, immersive and dark you can almost feel the chill in the air and smell crispy leaves 🍁 Nor does she shy away from portraying the dark side of humanity.<br /><br />This was by far my <i>favorite</i> book of the series and I enjoyed every bit of it! <br /><br />I loved the close friendship between Kaye and Corny, and their shared grief of Janet. I loved the support they gave each other in dealing with their different traumas that occurred in <i>Tithe</i>. Their jokes, their understanding of each other’s quirks. It was just so sweet and I loved it.<br /><br />For the first time in this series I really liked Ellen’s character. She surprised me with how she handled things, but I loved her for it.<br /><br />I of course loved my beloved Roiben, and sympathized for all he had to put up with just to keep a dictator from having complete dominion of all of faerieland. I need to find my Roiben in real life 🥰<br /><br />The plot of this one had me hooked and had no dull blah moments like <i>Valiant</i> had. This one was soooo good! The definite best of the series! I’m so glad I read it and endured the ho-hum-ness of the previous books. I did like parts of both the first books, but this one I enjoyed in its entirety. Not as much as <i>Folk of the Air</i> obviously, but for her early writing, it’s a very enjoyable read 😊 </span>

<div id="review_23071245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23071245" />
    <a title="Res" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56479-res"><img alt="Res" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23071245?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Res" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Res" href="/user/show/56479-res">Res</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56479-res?shelf=sff">sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56479-res?shelf=slash-interest">slash-interest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23071245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4077981404669220333">Sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe_A_Modern_Faerie_Tale__Book_1_' title='Tithe A Modern Faerie Tale (Book 1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a>. The one where Roiben of the Seelie Court finds himself in charge of the Unseelie, and tries to protect his love Kaye, a pixie changeling, by giving her an impossible quest.<br/><br/>I really want to know what I'm doing wrong that I keep checking out books without knowing that they're sequels. Wouldn't you think they'd say so on the cover? <br/><br/>The backstory/exposition was very skillfully done here (unlike <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely__Wicked_Lovely___1_' title='Wicked Lovely (Wicked Lovely, #1) by Melissa Marr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wicked Lovely</a>, this book understands the difference between suspense and confusion), so i</span>
  <span id="freeText4077981404669220333" style="display:none">Sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe_A_Modern_Faerie_Tale__Book_1_" title="Tithe A Modern Faerie Tale (Book 1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a>. The one where Roiben of the Seelie Court finds himself in charge of the Unseelie, and tries to protect his love Kaye, a pixie changeling, by giving her an impossible quest.<br /><br />I really want to know what I'm doing wrong that I keep checking out books without knowing that they're sequels. Wouldn't you think they'd say so on the cover? <br /><br />The backstory/exposition was very skillfully done here (unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely__Wicked_Lovely___1_" title="Wicked Lovely (Wicked Lovely, #1) by Melissa Marr" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked Lovely</a>, this book understands the difference between suspense and confusion), so it wasn't too bad reading book 2 before book 1.<br /><br />I found Kaye reasonably believable and likeable, and I only wanted to throttle her a little bit for getting into trouble for lack of asking simple and obvious questions. I couldn't quite get a handle on Corny's character, and this might be a place where I'm paying the price for not having read Tithe yet, because I can't make sense of the cruel streak he shows every now and then. (Also, I'm not sure I really believe how quickly and totally he turns around, and how small a thing it takes to be the catalyst for the change.)<br /><br />Nice sexual tension between Corny and his male friend, and yay! for gay sexual tension without a big deal made of it.<br /><br />I liked the Faerie politics (except how Kaye solved the quest problem, which disappointed me). But the cruelty of the faeries is portrayed with more relish than I'm comfortable with; it came close to triggering my torture squick in a couple of places. And I'm not clear on the difference between the Seelie and Unseelie courts, though it seems very important to the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4077981404669220333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3247346275" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3247346275" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3247346275?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3rd-person">3rd-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-boi">mc-boi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=butt-ugly-covers">butt-ugly-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-gurl">mc-gurl</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3247346275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7753252769792727622">This was both better and way way way worse than the first book. I won’t even compare it to the second (yikes)<br/><br/>As usual, the pacing was atrocious, with hardly any coherent transitions at all; a lot of the story was just left for me to figure out on my own, I guess. Characters would change location at the drop of a hat without any preamble or explanation. It killed any flow or suspense or tension the story had managed to garner and left me bored and confused, and only wishing it would end faster.<br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText7753252769792727622" style="display:none">This was both better and way way way worse than the first book. I won’t even compare it to the second (yikes)<br /><br />As usual, the pacing was atrocious, with hardly any coherent transitions at all; a lot of the story was just left for me to figure out on my own, I guess. Characters would change location at the drop of a hat without any preamble or explanation. It killed any flow or suspense or tension the story had managed to garner and left me bored and confused, and only wishing it would end faster.<br /><br />The awkward instalove between Luis and Corny was super random, but since Luis was barely recognizable anyway, I guess it didn’t matter. (To be fair, Luis’ side of things felt a bit more natural, whereas it’s been established that Corny should be renamed Horny) Corny’s character arc came out of nowhere and also he never got any consequences for some very questionable decisions from the beginning of the book. Like, love can’t conquer all when one of the partners is a sociopath (looking at you, SJM 👀)<br /><br />Roiben’s plot was the more interesting storyline but also his character arc made no sense because he was barely in the book. If the book had been solely about him, it might have been better and had more room to expand on themes instead of mentioning them and moving on. Kaye’s storyline was mostly okay, but everything with her mom melted into saccharine mush, which was a real shame, since I had actually liked that part and even shed a single tear when she confronted her again. It had been really intriguing, but then Black took the easy route and decided to have an off-screen character arc for the mom and ruined the story. *sigh* It really could have been decent.<br /><br />Also, so many names were thrown around and I honestly don’t know if these characters had been introduced before or not, because they were treated like I already knew them and I definitely didn’t.<br /><br />This series was largely incoherent but 12 year old Faith probably would have been trash for it. Maybe I should have read this first so my expectations of Black’s work weren’t at least middling. The other two books I’ve read outside of this series (<i>
  <a href="https://youarewhat-youread.blogspot.com/2018/09/the-darkest-part-of-forest-holly-black.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkest Part of the Forest</a>
</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://youarewhat-youread.blogspot.com/2018/10/the-coldest-girl-in-coldtown-holly-black.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coldest Girl In Coldtown</a>
</i>) both weren’t great but I at least enjoyed them. Black has improved, I guess, but her books are still pretty and meaningless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7753252769792727622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49345803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49345803" />
    <a title="Wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow"><img alt="Wealhtheow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49345803?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wealhtheow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wealhtheow" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Bordertown, Charles De Lint, Emma Bull</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=pocmaincharacters">pocmaincharacters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=feypunk">feypunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=queer-characters">queer-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49345803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12625071029982659668">Ironside follows shortly after the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe_A_Modern_Faerie_Tale__Book_1_' title='Tithe A Modern Faerie Tale (Book 1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant_A_Modern_Tale_of_Faerie__Book_2_' title='Valiant A Modern Tale of Faerie (Book 2) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Valiant</a>. Roiben was a loyal knight of the Seelie Queen, even after she sent him to serve her sister, the Queen of the Unseelie Court. After countless years of torment and cruelty, he brought about the Unseelie Queen's death and now presides over her court. At his coronation, he sets an impossible quest for his lover, the pixie Kaye, to keep her safe from the war between the courts. Of course Kaye will have none of this romantic nonsense, and</span>
  <span id="freeText12625071029982659668" style="display:none">Ironside follows shortly after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe_A_Modern_Faerie_Tale__Book_1_" title="Tithe A Modern Faerie Tale (Book 1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant_A_Modern_Tale_of_Faerie__Book_2_" title="Valiant A Modern Tale of Faerie (Book 2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a>. Roiben was a loyal knight of the Seelie Queen, even after she sent him to serve her sister, the Queen of the Unseelie Court. After countless years of torment and cruelty, he brought about the Unseelie Queen's death and now presides over her court. At his coronation, he sets an impossible quest for his lover, the pixie Kaye, to keep her safe from the war between the courts. Of course Kaye will have none of this romantic nonsense, and pledges to fulfill his quest. Meanwhile, Kaye's bff Corny is dealing with the rage and self-loathing left behind by his enthrallment and his sister's death. <br /><br />This book feels so genuine. The characters are each and every one of them fully fleshed out--Corny is particularly real. The fey courts and the human world (aka "Ironside") are described with a precise poetry. Unlike Emma Bull's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/70582.War_for_the_Oaks" title="War for the Oaks by Emma Bull" rel="nofollow noopener">War for the Oaks</a> or say, Poppy Z Brite's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/452244.Lost_Souls" title="Lost Souls by Poppy Z. Brite" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost Souls</a>, the descriptions of the fey and the punked out humans never feel like wish-fulfillment. The entire book is about negotiation, re-negotiating power, trying to come to terms with an untenable situation and new, uncomfortable knowledge about oneself. I loved it! I read the entire book in about an hour.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12625071029982659668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_17159568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17159568" />
    <a title="Juushika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/616321-juushika"><img alt="Juushika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541586729p2/616321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17159568?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juushika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juushika" href="/user/show/616321-juushika">Juushika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=status-borrowed">status-borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17159568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer458893306099793375">A direct sequel to <i>Tithe</i>, <i>Ironside</i> picks up two months after <i>Tithe</i> left off. At Roiben's coronation as King of the Unseelie Court, Kaye, drunk on faerie wine, declares herself to Roiben, who in turn sends her on an impossible quest to prove her love to him. Meanwhile, Kaye decides to tell her mother that she is a changeling, and the Queen of the Seelie Court attacks Roiben, leading to a series of quests wherein Kaye must find her human double, find a way to save Roiben, and bring Roiben a faery </span>
  <span id="freeText458893306099793375" style="display:none">A direct sequel to <i>Tithe</i>, <i>Ironside</i> picks up two months after <i>Tithe</i> left off. At Roiben's coronation as King of the Unseelie Court, Kaye, drunk on faerie wine, declares herself to Roiben, who in turn sends her on an impossible quest to prove her love to him. Meanwhile, Kaye decides to tell her mother that she is a changeling, and the Queen of the Seelie Court attacks Roiben, leading to a series of quests wherein Kaye must find her human double, find a way to save Roiben, and bring Roiben a faery that can lie before she can see or speak to him again. Continuing with the vibrant magical atmosphere and faery world of <i>Tithe</i>, <i>Ironside</i> is the work of a much more mature and accomplished author: the characters are more realistically flawed while still being sympathetic, and the writing style is skillful and polished. Meanwhile, the story is still otherworldy, emotional, and honestly confronts difficult subjects. This book is not perfect, but it is a magical and enjoyable read, and I do recommend it.<br /><br />I should note here that I have not read <i>Valiant</i>, which falls between <i>Tithe</i> and <i>Ironside</i> in the series. However, these two books do make sense without <i>Valiant</i>.<br /><br />After reading <i>Tithe</i>, I had high hopes for <i>Ironside</i>. I hoped that it would have the same intense and well-conceived since of magic, but that it would exhibit Black's increased experience as a writer, and have better characters and a more polished style. I'm glad to say that my hopes were fulfilled on all accounts: <i>Ironside</i> contains all of the good qualities from <i>Tithe</i> and avoids many of the pitfalls of that first novel. The characters return, and continue with many of respective flaws: they drink and shoplift, they have deadbeat parents, they are immature and over-emotional. Yet these flaws are more realistic and the characters have gained good qualities. They have GEDs, they have real problems behind their emotional complaints, and they have become affectionate and sometimes even thoughtful. These are now characters that, however unusual or even non-human they may be, the reader can identify with, and the text benefits for it. The text also benefits from an experienced and matured writing style: the plot flows at a smoother pace and the climax and conclusion are better crafted and more complete, the repetition of phrases and actions is largely absent, and the overall text reads smoother and exhibits better editing. This book is written by an experienced author, and it is a sympathetic, well-paced, skillful piece of work.<br /><br />Alongside these clear improvements, the magical and human aspects of <i>Tithe</i> remain in all of their glory. Black's faeries are vividly conceived and described, from the grotesque and violent Unseelie Court to the apple blossom-strewn Seelie Court. Even better: The Unseelie Court now has a sympathetic ruler, and the Seelie Queen is a villain, adding realistic complication and interest to the darks and lights of faery politics. Kaye's search for her human double explores new aspects of Black's faery life and culture, as does the journeys of the two human characters, one of which desires to be more than human, the other of which hates faeries. The multiple quests of the plot are a classic storytelling structure, and they create subtle but important character growth in all of the main characters. Black does not try to avoid mature subjects, but rather explores everything from homosexuality to love to death in a way that is respectful, honest, and still appropriate to a young adult audience (that is, there are no explicit sex scenes or exceptional gruesome deaths). Both magical and distinctly human, <i>Ironside</i> is at once enjoyable and avidly readable as well as meaningful and personally relevant.<br /><br />While <i>Ironside</i> is by no means a perfect book (the characters and plot points are cliche, the dark court remains pointlessly dark, and Kaye and her friends in their personalities and experiences are not entirely realistic or deeply explored; all in all, it is not the most skillful or most memorable text), it is a great improvement and an enjoyable read. I believe that it makes more sense and is more enjoyable if the reader has already read at least <i>Tithe</i>, so pick up that book first. But <i>Ironside</i> shows a true step forward in Black's work as an author as well as being magical, meaningful, honest, edgy, and an approachable and swift read. I was happy that I picked up this book, and I do recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="458893306099793375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_4415494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4415494" />
    <a title="xnera" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/257961-xnera"><img alt="xnera" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4415494?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="xnera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="xnera" href="/user/show/257961-xnera">xnera</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4415494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1440848026926412679"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28867868.Old_Ironsides__Old_Ironsides__1_' title='Old Ironsides (Old Ironsides #1) by Dean Crawford' rel='nofollow noopener'> Ironside</a> is the third book in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'> Holly Black</a>'s Modern Faery series. I remember quite liking <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514627.Blood_Tithe__Blood_Tithe__1_' title='Blood Tithe (Blood Tithe #1) by Glenn J. Soucy' rel='nofollow noopener'> Tithe</a>, enough that I bought <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30375703.The_Valiant__The_Valiant___1_' title='The Valiant (The Valiant, #1) by Lesley Livingston' rel='nofollow noopener'> Valiant</a> when it came out in hardcover, which I also enjoyed, though not as much as the first. The world Black creates is intriguing. It's dark and gritty--these faeries ain't no Tinkerbell. In times it can almost feel <b>too</b> dark and disturbing, as the characters do their best to cause pain to others. There's always the bit of romance to offset the grittiness, though, and in fact</span>
  <span id="freeText1440848026926412679" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28867868.Old_Ironsides__Old_Ironsides__1_" title="Old Ironsides (Old Ironsides #1) by Dean Crawford" rel="nofollow noopener"> Ironside</a> is the third book in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener"> Holly Black</a>'s Modern Faery series. I remember quite liking <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13514627.Blood_Tithe__Blood_Tithe__1_" title="Blood Tithe (Blood Tithe #1) by Glenn J. Soucy" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tithe</a>, enough that I bought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30375703.The_Valiant__The_Valiant___1_" title="The Valiant (The Valiant, #1) by Lesley Livingston" rel="nofollow noopener"> Valiant</a> when it came out in hardcover, which I also enjoyed, though not as much as the first. The world Black creates is intriguing. It's dark and gritty--these faeries ain't no Tinkerbell. In times it can almost feel <b>too</b> dark and disturbing, as the characters do their best to cause pain to others. There's always the bit of romance to offset the grittiness, though, and in fact the touches of romance are my favorite parts of the series.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28867868.Old_Ironsides__Old_Ironsides__1_" title="Old Ironsides (Old Ironsides #1) by Dean Crawford" rel="nofollow noopener"> Ironside</a> is a perfectly capable book. It continually moves forward at a good pace, although a bit clumsily at times, especially in the segues. I found mostly having just a bit of confusion over what happened during these times before I was able to pick up the plot again. My biggest problem with the book, however, is that it failed to completely engage me. Why, I can't say for certain, but I had a sense that I was reading [b]about[/b] the characters, rather than living out their adventures with them. It's as if the book didn't get that one final polish that would make it shine.<br /><br />Still, it's a good story, and I did enjoy it. I plan on reading any subsequent books that come out, although I will probably wait for the paperbacks.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3311678255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3311678255" />
    <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger"><img alt="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603583342p2/67389898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3311678255?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger">Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781847380630" href="/book/show/3942410-ironside">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3311678255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3436385305680646955">If you already have an entire idea in your head of how you want a book to go, there's a pretty high chance that you'll be disappointed. After reading Tithe and being introduced to Kaye, I initially was surprised when Valiant introduced Val, but I quickly came to love her as much as Kaye. So for Book 3 I had this whole idea of two girls, going to Fairyland and kicking the Seelie Court's ass, fabulously. Which didn't happen.<br/><br/>If I hadn't of had an idea of how I wanted the book to go, I would have be</span>
  <span id="freeText3436385305680646955" style="display:none">If you already have an entire idea in your head of how you want a book to go, there's a pretty high chance that you'll be disappointed. After reading Tithe and being introduced to Kaye, I initially was surprised when Valiant introduced Val, but I quickly came to love her as much as Kaye. So for Book 3 I had this whole idea of two girls, going to Fairyland and kicking the Seelie Court's ass, fabulously. Which didn't happen.<br /><br />If I hadn't of had an idea of how I wanted the book to go, I would have been disappointed anyway. Sitting down now and thinking about what actually happened, I'm sat thinking, what actually happened? A big fat nothing for the most part, just Kaye thinking about Roiben, Corny being gay, and reintroducing Luis from Val's book, who I didn't care for.<br /><br />Val did make a very brief appearance at the end of the story for a couple of lines, which was a bitter disappointment and really made her book useless. This story also didn't have the grit that Tithe and Valiant had, after the drowning of Kaye's best friend and descriptions of drug use during the previous books, this one felt pretty mellow. Still, I'm interesting to see what happens to the Fae world and seeing Kaye and Roiben again during my re-read of The Cruel Prince, which I remember basically nothing about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3436385305680646955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19175547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19175547" />
    <a title="Cherie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019558-cherie"><img alt="Cherie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310255951p2/1019558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19175547?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cherie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cherie" href="/user/show/1019558-cherie">Cherie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19175547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10703590679850568358"><i>Ironside</i> is the third book in Holly Black's Faerie Tale series, though it's actually a continuation of book one, <a href='http://books.cheriepie.com/2007/04/32-tithe-modern-faerie-tale-by-holly.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Tithe</i>
</a>. The second book, <a href='http://books.cheriepie.com/2007/07/47-valiant-modern-tale-of-faerie-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Valiant</i>
</a>, takes place in the same world as books one and three but with different characters, some of which appear here as well. Kay and Roiben's stories however, are pretty much found only in books one and three. :)<br/><br/>Roiben is now King of the Unseelie Court, and against his wishes, Kaye has declared herself to him, thereby swearing loyalty to the Unseelie</span>
  <span id="freeText10703590679850568358" style="display:none"><i>Ironside</i> is the third book in Holly Black's Faerie Tale series, though it's actually a continuation of book one, <a href="http://books.cheriepie.com/2007/04/32-tithe-modern-faerie-tale-by-holly.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Tithe</i>
</a>. The second book, <a href="http://books.cheriepie.com/2007/07/47-valiant-modern-tale-of-faerie-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Valiant</i>
</a>, takes place in the same world as books one and three but with different characters, some of which appear here as well. Kay and Roiben's stories however, are pretty much found only in books one and three. :)<br /><br />Roiben is now King of the Unseelie Court, and against his wishes, Kaye has declared herself to him, thereby swearing loyalty to the Unseelie Court in the process... assuming that is, that she can complete the seemingly impossible quest set before her—find a faerie who can tell a lie. This book follows Kaye's adventures alongside her old friend Corny as they travel between the human and faerie realms, not necessarily keeping a low profile along the way. LOL<br /><br />I enjoyed this third book in the series and look forward to more of Ms. Black's Faerie Tale universe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10703590679850568358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pFaF9Sg9GOlgqXBv4Es1Cj242NXbsI5CdV2+lZKx2zbFyrFtqucX0urvgZRUKlKbiSYmBZtxVNJ4ER1r/lU7IQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer5727120093665150453">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house </span>
  <span id="freeText5727120093665150453" style="display:none">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house with a secret library.</span>
